                     <itype>8</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ائتمّهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [written with the disjunctive alif <foreign lang="ar">اِيتَمَّهُ</foreign>]: see 1, first sentence.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ائتمّ بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He followed his example; he imitated him; he did as he did, following his example;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">taking him as an example, an exemplar, a pattern,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an object of imitation;</hi> (S, Mgh, Msb;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1168-1" target="أَمَّهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n1162"/></foreign>: (Bd in xvi. 121:) the object of the verb is termed <foreign lang="ar">إِمَامٌ</foreign>; (S, M, Mgh, Msb, K;) applied to a learned man, (Msb,) or a head, chief, or leader, or some other person. (M, K.) <hi rend="ital">He made it an</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّة</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">إِمَّة</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">a way, course,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rule, of life</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conduct;</hi> as explained immediately before in the work whence this is taken]; as also <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1168-2" target="تأمّم" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>به</foreign>. (M.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">ائتمّ بِالشَّيْءِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ائْتَمَى به</foreign>, by substitution [of <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">م</foreign>], (M, K,) disapproving of the doubling [of the <foreign lang="ar">م</foreign>]. (M.)    </entryFree>29:T293e,<entryFree id="n1169" key="أَمْ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَمْ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is a conjunction, (S, M, K,) connected with what precedes it (Msb, Mughnee) so that neither what precedes it nor what follows it is independent, the one of the other. (Mughnee.) It denotes interrogation; (M, K;) or is used in a case of interrogation, (S, Msb,) corresponding to the interrogative <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign>, and meaning <foreign lang="ar">أَىّ</foreign>, (S,) or, as Z says, <foreign lang="ar">أَىُّ الأَمْرَيْنِ كَائِنٌ</foreign>; [for an explanation of which, see what follows;] (Mughnee;) or, [in other words,] corresponding to the interrogative <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign>, whereby, and by <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ</foreign>, one seeks, or desires, particularization: (Mughnee:) it is as though it were an interrogative after an interrogative. (Lth, T.) Thus you say, <foreign lang="ar">أَزَيُدٌ فِى الدَّارِ أَمْ عَمْرٌو</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is Zeyd in the house, or 'Amr?</hi>]; (S, Mughnee;) i. e. which of them two (<foreign lang="ar">أَيُّهُمَا</foreign>) is in the house? (S;) therefore what follows <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign> and what precedes it compose one sentence; and it is not used in commanding nor in forbidding; and what follows it must correspond to what precedes it in the quality of noun and of verb; so that you say, <foreign lang="ar">أَزَيْدٌ قَائِمٌ أَمع قَاعِدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is Zeyd standing, or sitting?</hi>] and <foreign lang="ar">أَقَامَ زَيْدٌ أَمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَعَدَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Did Zeyd stand, or sit?</hi>]. (Msb.) It is not to be coupled with <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign> after it: you may not say, <foreign lang="ar">أَعِنْدَكَ زَيْدٌ أَمْ أَعِنْدَكَ عَمْرٌو</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  As connected in like manner with what goes before, it is preceded by <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign> denoting equality [by occurring after <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءٌ</foreign> &amp;c.], and corresponds thereto, as in [the Kur lxiii. 6,] <foreign lang="ar">سَوَآءُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَسْتَغْفَرْتَ لَهُمٌ لَمٌ تَسْتَغُفِرْ لَهُمٌ</foreign> [It will be <hi rend="ital">equal to them whether thou beg forgiveness for them or do not beg forgiveness for them</hi>]. (Mughnee.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  It is also unconnected with what precedes it, (S, Msb, Mughnee,) implying always digression, (Mughnee,) preceded by an enunciative, or an interrogative, (S, Msb, Mughnee,) other than <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign>, (Mughnee,) or by <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign> not meant [really] as an interrogative but to denote disapproval, (Mughnee,) and signifies <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ</foreign>, (Lth, Zj, T, S, M, Mughnee, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign> together, (Msb,) and this is its meaning always accord. to all the Basrees, but the Koofees deny this. (Mughnee.) Thus, using it after an enunciative, you say, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّهَا لَإِبِلٌ أَمْ شَآءٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily they are camels: nay,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nay but, they are sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nay, are they sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goats?</hi>]: (S Msb, Mughnee:) this being said when one looks at a bodily form, and imagines it to be a number of camels, and says what first occurs to him; then the opinion that it is a number of sheep or goats suggests itself to him, and he turns from the first idea, and says, <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ شَآءٌ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ</foreign>, because it is a digression from what precedes it; though what follows <foreign lang="ar">بل</foreign> is [properly] a thing known certainly, and what follows <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign> is opined. (S, TA.) And using it after an interrogative in this case, you say, <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ زيْدٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مُنْطَلِقٌ أَمْ عَمْرٌو</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is Zeyd going away? Nay rather,</hi> or, <hi rend="ital">or rather, is 'Amr?</hi>]: you digress from the question respecting Zeyd's going away, and make the question to relate to 'Amr; so that <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign> implies indecisive opinion, and interrogation, and digression. (S.) And thus using it, you say, <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ زَيْدٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَامَ أَمْ عَمْرٌو</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Did Zeyd stand? Nay rather,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">or rather, did 'Amr?</hi>]. (Msb.) And an ex. of the same is the saying [in the Kur xiii. 17], <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ يَسْتَوِى الْأَعْمَى وَالْبَصِيرُ أَمْ هَلْ تَسْتَوِى الظُّلُمَاتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَالنُّورُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Are the blind and the seeing equal? Or rather are darkness and light equal?</hi>]. (Mughnee.) And an ex. of it preceded by <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign> used to denote disapproval is the saying [in the Kur vii. 194], <foreign lang="ar">أَلَهُمْ أَرْجُلٌ يَمْشُونَ بِهَا أَمْ لَهُمْ أَيْدٍ يَبْطِشُونَ بِهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Have they feet, to walk therewith? Or have they hands to assault therewith?</hi>]: for <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign> is here equivalent to a negation. (Mughnee.) [It has been shown above that] <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ</foreign> is sometimes introduced immediately before <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ</foreign>: (S, K:) but IB says that this is when <foreign lang="ar">هل</foreign> occurs in a phrase next before it; [as in the ex. from the Kur xiii. 17, cited above;] and in this case, the interrogative meaning of <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign> is annulled; it being introduced only to denote a digression. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  It is also used as a simple interrogative; accord. to the assertion of AO; in <pb n="89"/> the sense of <foreign lang="ar">هَلْ</foreign>; (Mughnee;) or in the sense of the interrogative <foreign lang="ar">أَ</foreign>; (Lth, T, K) as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">أَمْ عِنْدَكَ غَدَآءِ حَاضِرٌ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Hast thou a morning-meal ready?</hi> a good form of speech used by the Arabs; (Lth, T;) and allowable when preceded by another phrase. (T.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And sometimes it is redundant; (AZ, T, S, Mughnee, K) in the dial. of the people of El-Yemen; (T;) as in the saying, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَا دَهْنَ أَمْ مَا كَانَ مَشْيِى رقَصَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بَلْ قَدْ تَكُونُ مِشْيَتِى تَوَقُّصَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (T, S, * [in the latter, <foreign lang="ar">يا هِنْدُ</foreign>, and only the former hemistich is given,]) meaning <hi rend="ital">O Dahnà,</hi> (the curtailed form <foreign lang="ar">دَهْنَ</foreign> being used for <foreign lang="ar">دَهْنَآء</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">my walking was not,</hi> as now in my age, [a feeble movement like] <hi rend="ital">dancing: but</hi> in my youth, <hi rend="ital">my manner of walking used to be a bounding:</hi> (T:) this is accord. to the opinion of AZ: but accord. to another opinion, <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign> is here [virtually] conjoined with a preceding clause which is suppressed; as though the speaker had said, <foreign lang="ar">يَا دَهْنَ أَكَانَ مَشْيِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَقَصَّا أَمْ مَا كَانَ كَذلِكَ</foreign>. (A 'Hát, TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  It is also used (T, Mughnee) in the dial. of the people of El-Yemen, (T,) or of Teiyi and Himyer, (Mughnee,) in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>, (T,) to render a noun determinate. (Mughnee.) So in the trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ مِنَ امْبِرّ امْصِيامُ فِى امْسَفَرِ</foreign>, (T, Mughnee,) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">الَيْسَ مِنَ البِرِّ الصِّيَامُ فِى السَّفَرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Fasting in journeying is not</hi> an act <hi rend="ital">of obedience</hi> to God]. (T, and M in art. <foreign lang="ar">بر</foreign>.) So too in the trad., <foreign lang="ar">اَلْآنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">طَابَ امْضَرْبُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Now fighting has become lawful;</hi> as related accord. to the dial. of Himyer, for <foreign lang="ar">الضَّرْبُ</foreign>. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">طيب</foreign>.) It has been said that this form <foreign lang="ar">ام</foreign> is only used in those cases in which the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> of the article does not become incorporated into the first letter of the noun to which it is prefixed; as in the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">خُذِ الرُّمْحَ وَارْكَبِ امْفَرَسَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Take thou the spear, and mount the mare,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">horse</hi>], related as heard in El-Yemen; but this usage may be peculiar to some of the people of that country; not common to all of them; as appears from what we have cited above. (Mughnee.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَمَ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">أَمَا</foreign>, before an oath: see art. <foreign lang="ar">اما</foreign>.       <sense type="A" n="4">-A4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">أَمَ اللّٰهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَمُ اللّٰهِ</foreign> &amp;c.: see <foreign lang="ar">أَيْمُنُ اللّٰهِ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">يمن</foreign>.    </entryFree>2a:T4499,<entryFree id="n1170" key="أُمٌّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أُمٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A mother</hi> (T, S, M, Msb, K, &amp;c.) [of a human being and] of any animal; (IAar, T;) as also ↓<foreign lang="ar">إِمٌّ</foreign>, (Sb, M, Msb, K) and ↓<foreign lang="ar">إُمَّةٌ</foreign>, (T, M, Msb, K,) and ↓<foreign lang="ar">أُمَّهَةٌ</foreign>, (S, M, Msb, K,) which last is the original form (S, Msb) accord. to some, (Msb,) or the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> in this is augmentative (M, Msb) accord. to others: (Msb:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّهَاتٌ</foreign> (Lth, T, S, M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّاتٌ</foreign>; (S, M, Msb, K;) or the former is applied to human beings, and the latter to beasts; (T, S;) or the former to rational beings, and the latter to irrational; (M, K;) or the former is much applied to human beings, and the latter to others, for the sake of distinction; (Msb;) but the reverse is sometimes the case: (IB:) IDrst and others hold the latter to be of weak authority: (TA:) the dim. of <foreign lang="ar">أُمٌّ</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1170-1" target="أُمَيْمَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n1180"/></foreign> (T, S, K) accord. to some of the Arabs; but correctly, [accord. to those who hold the original form of <foreign lang="ar">أُمٌّ</foreign> to be <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّهَةٌ</foreign>,] it is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1170-2" target="أُمَيْمِهَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (Lth, T, TA. [In a copy of the T, I find this latter form of the dim. written <foreign lang="ar">اميهة</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّ لَكَ</foreign> denotes dispraise; (S;) being used by the Arabs as meaning <hi rend="ital">Thou hast no</hi> free, or ingenuous, <hi rend="ital">mother;</hi> because the sons of female slaves are objects of dispraise with the Arabs; and is only said in anger and reviling: (A Heyth, T:) or, as some say, it means <hi rend="ital">thou art one</hi> who has been picked up as a foundling, <hi rend="ital">having no</hi> Known <hi rend="ital">mother:</hi> (TA:) [or] it is also sometimes used in praise; (A 'Obeyd, T, S, K;) and is used as an imprecation without the desire of its being fulfilled upon the person addressed, being said in vehemence of love; [lit. meaning <hi rend="ital">mayest thou have no mother!</hi>], like <foreign lang="ar">ثَكِلَتْكَ أُمُّكَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَبَا لَكَ</foreign>, [and <foreign lang="ar">قَاتَلَكَ اللّٰهُ</foreign>,] &amp;c. (Har p. 165.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Some elide the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> of <foreign lang="ar">أُمّ</foreign>; as in the saying of 'Adee Ibn—Zeyd. <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَيُّهَا العَائِبُ عِنْدِمَّ زَيْدٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">O thou who art blaming in my presence the mother of Zeyd</hi>]; meaning, <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدِى أُمَّ زَيْدٍ</foreign>; the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> of <foreign lang="ar">عندى</foreign> being also elided on account of the occurrence of two quiescent letters [after the elision of the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> of <foreign lang="ar">أُمّ</foreign>]: (Lth, T, S:) and as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">وَيْلُمِّهِ</foreign>, (S,) which means <foreign lang="ar">وَيْلٌ لِأُمِّهِ</foreign>. (S, and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">ويل</foreign>, q. v.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا أُمَّاكّ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">They two are thy two parents:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thy mother and thy maternal aunt.</hi> (K.) [But] <foreign lang="ar">فَدَّاهُ بِأُمَّيْهِ</foreign> is said to mean [<hi rend="ital">He expressed a wish that he</hi> (another) <hi rend="ital">might be ransomed with</hi>] <hi rend="ital">his mother and his grandmother.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  One says also, <foreign lang="ar">يَا <ref cref="n1170-3" target="أُمَّتِ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>لَا تَفْعَلِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O my mother, do not thou</hi> such a thing], and [in like manner] <foreign lang="ar">يَا أَبَتِ افْعَلْ</foreign>; making the sign of the fem. gender a substitute for the [pronominal] affix <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>; and in a case of pause, you say <foreign lang="ar">يَا أُمَّهْ</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  And one says, <foreign lang="ar">مَا أُمِّى وَأُمُّهُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">مَا شَكْلِى وَشَكْلُهُ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">What relationship have I to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it?</hi> or <hi rend="ital">what concern have I with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it?</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">what is my case and</hi> [what is] <hi rend="ital">his</hi> or <hi rend="ital">its, case?</hi> because of his, or its, remoteness from me: whence, (T,) <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَمَا أُمِّى وَأُمُّ الوَحْشِ لَمَّا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">تَفَرَّعَ فِى مَفَارِقِىَ الْمَشِيبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And what concern have I with the wild animals when hoariness hath spread in the places where my hair parts?</hi>]; (T, S;) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مَا أَنَاوَطَلَبُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الوَحْشِ بَعْدَ مَا كَبِرْتُ</foreign> [i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مَا أمْرِي وَطَلَبُ الوَحْشِ</foreign>: in one copy of the S, <foreign lang="ar">وَطَلَبَ</foreign>, i. e. with <foreign lang="ar">وَ</foreign> as a prep. denoting concomitance, and therefore governing the accus. case: both readings virtually meaning <hi rend="ital">what concern have I with the pursuing of the wild animals after I have grown old?</hi>]: he means, the girls: and the mention of <foreign lang="ar">أُمّ</foreign> in the verse is superfluous. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أُمٌّ</foreign> also relates to inanimate things that have growth; as in <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ الشَّجَرَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The mother of the tree</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ النَّخْلَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the mother of the palm-tree</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ المَوْزِةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the mother of the banana-tree;</hi> of which see an ex. in art. <foreign lang="ar">موز</foreign>]; and the like. (M, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  And it signifies also The <hi rend="ital">source, origin, foundation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">basis,</hi> (S, M, Msb, K,) of a thing, (S, Msb, [in the former of which, this is the first of the meanings assigned to the word,]) or of anything; (M, K) its <hi rend="ital">stay, support,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">efficient cause of subsistence.</hi> (M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Anything to which other things are collected together,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adjoined:</hi> (IDrd, M, K:) <hi rend="ital">anything to which the other things that are next thereto are collected together,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adjoined:</hi> (Lth, T:) the <hi rend="ital">main,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">chief, part</hi> of a thing; the <hi rend="ital">main body</hi> thereof: and that which is <hi rend="ital">a compriser,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">comprehender,</hi> of [other] things: (Ham p. 44:) the <hi rend="ital">place of collection, comprisal,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">comprehension,</hi> of a thing; the <hi rend="ital">place of combination</hi> thereof. (En-Nadr, T.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  And hence, (IDrd, M,) The <hi rend="ital">head,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">chief,</hi> of a people, or company of men; (IDrd, S, M, K;) because others collect themselves together to him: (IDrd, TA:) so in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ عِيَالٍ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">the mother of a household</hi>], in a poem of Esh-Shenfarà: (IDrd, M:) or in this instance, it has the signification next following, accord. to Esh-Sháfi'ee. (T.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A man who has the charge of the food and service</hi> of a people, or company of men; accord. to EshSháfi'ee: (T:) or their <hi rend="ital">servant.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  A man's <hi rend="ital">aged wife.</hi> (IAar, T, K.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A place of habitation</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode.</hi> (K.) So in the Kur [ci. 6], <foreign lang="ar">فَأُمُّهُ هَاوِيَةٌ</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">العَرَبِ</foreign>; because most of the Arabs were of this description: (Msb:) the art of writing was known among the Arabs [in the time of Mohammad] by the people of Et-Táïf, who learned it from a man of the people of El-Heereh, and these had it from the people of El-Ambár. (T.) <foreign lang="ar">أُمِّيُّون لَا يَعْلَمُونَ</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">الكِتَابَ</foreign>, in the Kur ii. 73, means <hi rend="ital">Vulgar persons,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">heathen,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">who know not the Book of the Law revealed to Moses:</hi> (Jel:) or <hi rend="ital">ignorant persons, who know not writing,</hi> so that they may read that book; or, <hi rend="ital">who know not the Book of the Law revealed to Moses.</hi> (Bd.) Mohammad was termed <foreign lang="ar">أُمِّىّ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">A Gentile,</hi> as distinguished from an Israelite: or, accord. to most of his followers, meaning <hi rend="ital">illiterate;</hi>] because the nation (<foreign lang="ar">أُمَّة</foreign>) of the Arabs did not write, nor read writing; and [they say that] God sent him as an apostle when he did not write, nor read from a book; and this natural condition of his was one of his miraculous signs, to which reference is made in the Kur [xxix. 47], where it is said, “thou didst not read, before it, from a book, nor didst thou write it with thy right hand:” (T, TA:) but accord. to the more correct opinion, he was not well acquainted with written characters nor with poetry, but he discriminated between good and bad poetry: or, as some assert, he became acquainted with writing after he had been unacquainted therewith, on account of the expression “ before it ” in the verse of the Kur mentioned above: or, as some say, this may mean that he wrote though ignorant of the art of writing, like as some of the kings, being <foreign lang="ar">أُمِّيُّون</foreign>, write their signs, or marks: (TA:) or, accord. to Jaafar Es-Sádik, he used to read from the book, or scripture, if he did not write. (Kull p. 73.)                   </form> The <hi rend="ital">quality denoted by the epithet</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أُمِّىٌّ</foreign>: (TA:) [<hi rend="ital">gentilism: <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> heathenism:</hi> &amp;c.:] <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> the <hi rend="ital">quality of being</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in the natural condition of the nation to which one belongs,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">as brought forth by one's mother, in respect of not having learned the art of writing nor the reading thereof.</hi> (Kull p. 73.) <foreign lang="ar">أُمَّانٌ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">أُمِّىٌّ</foreign>; and see also art. <foreign lang="ar">امن</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ الدِّمَاغِ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) or, [which means the same,] <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ الرَّأْسِ</foreign>, (M, K,) <hi rend="ital">so that there remains between it and the brain [only] a thin skin:</hi> (S:) it is the most severe of <foreign lang="ar">شِجَاج</foreign> [except that which reaches the brain (see <foreign lang="ar">شَجَّةٌ</foreign>)]: ISk says that the person suffering from it roars, or bellows, (<foreign lang="ar">يَصْعَقُ</foreign>,) like thunder, and like the braying of camels, and is unable to go forth into the sun: (Msb:) the mulct for it is one third of the whole price of blood: (TA:) IAar assigns the meaning of [this kind of] <foreign lang="ar">شَجَّة</foreign> to
